  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_178443ef-6e5b-4b2e-87d8-77a5a34eb676'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2870999159901762550">Overflowing with all of the majesty and intrigue of medieval glory days, this magnificent New York Times bestseller is a page-turner of passion and loyalty, justice and honor. Beloved storyteller Julie Garwood steps back to the silver-shrouded Highlands of her classic tale The Secret--and hails the return of two unforgettable warriors: Ramsey Sinclair and Brodick Buchanan.</span>
  <span id="freeText2870999159901762550" style="display:none">Overflowing with all of the majesty and intrigue of medieval glory days, this magnificent New York Times bestseller is a page-turner of passion and loyalty, justice and honor. Beloved storyteller Julie Garwood steps back to the silver-shrouded Highlands of her classic tale The Secret--and hails the return of two unforgettable warriors: Ramsey Sinclair and Brodick Buchanan. In the dark days after the death of Richard the Lionhearted, lives and lands would fall into upheaval at the hands of a power-hungry British ruler and his violent minions. One victim of the scourge is innocent Gillian, who is a mere child when the cruel and ambitious Baron Alford slaughters her father and tears her family apart. Alford, determined to recover a jeweled box for the despotic King John, is furious when the precious treasure slips through his fingers--only to be lost for more than a decade.<br /><br />Now a beautiful young woman, Gillian finds the key to resolving her past in handsome Scottish chieftains Ramsey Sinclair and Brodick Buchanan. With the cunning and courage of the daring Scotsmen, and with the friendship of a new ally, Bridgid KirkConnell, Gillian at last fights the unscrupulous Baron Alford, laying claim to her home, her family, and her father's reputation. But in the presence of the mighty warriors, Gillian and Bridgid discover that desire can be a weapon of conquest...betrayal can slay trust in a heartbeat...and the greatest risk of all is surrender--to the deep emotions of unexpected love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2870999159901762550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession"><img alt="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511556834p2/28967089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1873426629?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession">Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=own-book">own-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873426629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14282527513990885730">I'm going to keep this short and sweet! I loved this book too. I have pretty much loved every Julie Garwood book I have read so far. This book was like two love stories in one. The main love story was Gillian and Brodick. The other love story was a small side story that I felt really should have been it's own book. That side love story was Ramsey and Bridgid. I loved Brodick from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_' title='The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1312123398s/107770.jpg' alt='The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> and he was amazing in this book. He was so rough, hard, kick ass, and so damn prefect that I just love the hell </span>
  <span id="freeText14282527513990885730" style="display:none">I'm going to keep this short and sweet! I loved this book too. I have pretty much loved every Julie Garwood book I have read so far. This book was like two love stories in one. The main love story was Gillian and Brodick. The other love story was a small side story that I felt really should have been it's own book. That side love story was Ramsey and Bridgid. I loved Brodick from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_" title="The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1312123398s/107770.jpg" alt="The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> and he was amazing in this book. He was so rough, hard, kick ass, and so damn prefect that I just love the hell outta him. Gillian was brave, sweet and outspoken. I love outspoken heroines that don't let men walk on them. Gillian didn't let Brodick walk all over her. I loved them as a couple and I loved every minute of their love story. I really wish they didn't have to share their pages with another couple. Then I could have had more time with them. Also Ramsey and Bridgid were so likable they should have gotten their own book. I wanted more time with them too. I loved the plot and I loved that the bad guys got theirs. This book was great!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14282527513990885730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13497381564201738631">Oh, crap. Did I really give this <b>5 stars</b> the first time I read it?<br/><b>Has this <i>really</i> been sitting on my <i>favorites</i> shelf?!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447262761ra/16977868.gif' width='250' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>See? <i>This</i> is why it's dangerous to do rereads.<br/><i>sigh</i><br/>So, 5 years ago, I read this and thought it was <b>A-MAZING</b>.<br/>Like, the <i>bestest</i> book evah! And I've been singing its praises ever since.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447263396ra/16977909.gif' width='400' height='170' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In fact, when I saw it was on sale a while back, I bought it!<br/>Those of you who know me realize what a big deal that was. For those of you who don't? Let's just say...I'm cheap. <s>Reallyreallyreally cheap!</s></span>
  <span id="freeText13497381564201738631" style="display:none">Oh, crap. Did I really give this <b>5 stars</b> the first time I read it?<br><b>Has this <i>really</i> been sitting on my <i>favorites</i> shelf?!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447262761ra/16977868.gif" width="250" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>See? <i>This</i> is why it's dangerous to do rereads.<br><i>sigh</i><br>So, 5 years ago, I read this and thought it was <b>A-MAZING</b>.<br>Like, the <i>bestest</i> book evah! And I've been singing its praises ever since.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447263396ra/16977909.gif" width="400" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In fact, when I saw it was on sale a while back, I bought it!<br>Those of you who know me realize what a big deal that was. For those of you who don't? Let's just say...I'm cheap. <s>Reallyreallyreally cheap!</s><br><i>It wouldn't be an exaggeration to say I guard my money like that shriveled-up hobbit thing from Lord of the Rings.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447263725ra/16977915.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, I went into this expecting to feel...<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447264101ra/16977940.gif" width="370" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And, instead, I felt more...<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447264101ra/16977941.gif" width="370" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not sure <i>what</i> happened here, but, this time around, I thought the dialogue was kinda clunky. Plus, there were several times I had to put it down, because it just wasn't holding my attention the way I had hoped.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447264734ra/16977999.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the <i>romance</i> was...WTF?<br>What the hell was I <i>thinking</i> when I read this originally?!<br>I sorta wanted to grab hold of my younger self, and ask her a few questions...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447264734ra/16978000.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't mind when guys aren't <i>perfect</i> in romance novels. I like tough guys, snarky guys, even rude guys! <br>But you've gotta give me <i>some reason</i> to root for them.<br>This guy?<br><i>Ehhhhhhhh.</i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447265828ra/16978094.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm <b>not</b> saying he was a villainous, horrible person! <br>Just...I didn't like him very much. <br>He was a cookie-cutter version of every emotionally retarded <i>hero</i> ever put on paper.<br>And I was not all that impressed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447265828ra/16978095.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean, it was still a <i>decent</i> book, and I was entertained enough to finish it, but I was pretty underwhelmed. <br>Thing is, I had such fond memories of this book! Ugh. <br>I think it's gonna take me a while to get over the disappointment.<br><i>sobs</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447266568ra/16978203.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_45263939" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45263939" />
    <a title="Dina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1918270-dina"><img alt="Dina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460302951p2/1918270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45263939?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina" href="/user/show/1918270-dina">Dina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=dik">dik</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45263939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6876229262825009022">This was only my 2nd book by Julie Garwood, following <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_' title='The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret</a>, and I think I found a new (to me) author to glom. I just <i>loved</i> these books!<br/><br/>Brodick Buchanan was a secondary character in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_' title='The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret</a> that had "hero" tattooed on his forehead, so I was more than happy when I found out that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107776.Ransom__Highlands__Lairds___2_' title='Ransom (Highlands' Lairds, #2) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ransom</a> was "his" book. He was the typical alpha hero and we all know what happens when this kind fall in love. They fall hard and forever, but not always have the grace of acknowledging the fall, LOL. Brodick was </span>
  <span id="freeText6876229262825009022" style="display:none">This was only my 2nd book by Julie Garwood, following <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_" title="The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret</a>, and I think I found a new (to me) author to glom. I just <i>loved</i> these books!<br /><br />Brodick Buchanan was a secondary character in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_" title="The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret</a> that had "hero" tattooed on his forehead, so I was more than happy when I found out that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107776.Ransom__Highlands__Lairds___2_" title="Ransom (Highlands' Lairds, #2) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">Ransom</a> was "his" book. He was the typical alpha hero and we all know what happens when this kind fall in love. They fall hard and forever, but not always have the grace of acknowledging the fall, LOL. Brodick was just like that, and it was funny to see him trying to deal with it. When he <i>told</i> Gillian that <i>she</i> loved <i>him</i>, I giggled like a schoolgirl. And when he tricked her into marrying him, I laughed like a lunatic. That was one short-lived Big Misunderstanding I had no problem with. <i>"On a horse? I was married on a horse?"</i> Too funny! I doubt Brodick would get away with his antics in real life but he just turned out to be one of my favorite heroes in Romancelandia.<br /><br />Gillian was perfect match for Brodick. She didn't need to be coddled, which was refreshing when it comes to heroines in Romancelandia. Not that she was harsh or anything like that, she was just strong and independent. And yet, once she fell in love with Brodick, she wasn't afraid to admit she <i>needed</i> him to make her happier and she enjoyed talking and sharing her feelings with him. If I have a minor quibble about her, it's her behavior near the end of the story, when she almost drove her uncle crazy with her crying over Brodick: it was a bit out of character but, all things considered, it didn't bother me much. It did make me smile imagining her uncle's "suffering". :)<br /><br />As for the plot, I was a little confused in the beginning: there were so many players and so much going on that I felt kind of dizzy. Why hadn't Gillian been killed by the villainous Baron Alford? Was Gillian's sister truly alive? How did Gillian and Alec meet considering how prisoners are supposed to be kept isolated? So many questions... Thankfully, everything started making sense soon enough and there was no stopping after that. Great story!<br /><br />There was a secondary love story involving Ramsey Sinclair, a friend of Brodick's who also appeared in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_" title="The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret</a>, and Bridgid, a member of the Sinclair clan. It was nice, funny but underdeveloped. Ramsey and Bridgid were very interesting characters, their (few) interactions were funny and entertaining, and I think they deserved a book fully dedicated to telling their story. I didn't get to see the build-up of their relationship, especially on Ramsey's side, so it was kind of disappointing to see their HEA crammed into Brodick and Gillian's.<br /><br />This was a long book (546 pages) but, frankly, it didn't feel like it. It was filled with romance (duh!), humor, action, intrigue, suspense, some angst, and wonderful characters that I couldn't help but love. A true keeper!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6876229262825009022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=medium-steam">medium-steam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=spunky-heroine">spunky-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-secondary-characters">fabulous-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-hero">fabulous-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-characters">fabulous-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-characterizations">fabulous-characterizations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173710476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2676820773649953252"><b>4 to 4 1/2 stars</b><br/><br/><i>Ransom</i> is the follow-up book to <i>The Secret</i> and it definitely exceeded my expectations. Not only did it include the secondary characters I loved but also gave me a hero and heroine I could fall in love with and a romance over which I could swoon. Like <i>The Secret</i>, this book focuses on the overall plot rather than just romance. Fortunately, the love story and chemistry between Brodick and Gillian more than makes up for it. <br/><br/>Interestingly, it was a five year old "wanna be Highlander w</span>
  <span id="freeText2676820773649953252" style="display:none"><b>4 to 4 1/2 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Ransom</i> is the follow-up book to <i>The Secret</i> and it definitely exceeded my expectations. Not only did it include the secondary characters I loved but also gave me a hero and heroine I could fall in love with and a romance over which I could swoon. Like <i>The Secret</i>, this book focuses on the overall plot rather than just romance. Fortunately, the love story and chemistry between Brodick and Gillian more than makes up for it. <br /><br />Interestingly, it was a five year old "wanna be Highlander warrior" name Alec (the son of Iain and Judith from <i>The Secret</i>) who stole my heart and the story. He was endearing, inquisitive, and adorably obnoxious with his continual questions of "you know what?" You just had to love him!<br /><br />Brodick and Gillian were strong and likable characters. They complemented each other perfectly and their chemistry radiated off the pages. I found myself eagerly looking forward to their heart-warming and witty interactions.<br /><br />Brodick is a hero to swoon over. He was my favorite male character in <i>The Secret</i>. I had a feeling that once I read <i>Ransom</i>, he would become my all-time favorite Julie Garwood hero. And boy was I right! He's your true blue alpha hero, with all the strengths and weakness that encompass that aggressive but admirable personality. I was grateful that Julie Garwood kept Brodick, regardless of his feelings and love for Gillian, true to his character traits throughout the book. <br /><br />I can't help but smile when I think of Gillian’s character. She's a fabulous and endearing heroine. I liked her spunk, confidence, determination, kindness, and heroism, even though she had a few of those “too stupid to live” moments.<br /><br />In my opinion, Julie Garwood has a way of creating the most lovable and endearing heroines I’ve read. There isn’t a Julie Garwood book I’ve read where I didn’t completely fall in love with her wonderfully spunky and engaging heroines. True, they may be borderline Pollyanna, but that’s okay. They’re all written with such heart and soul you simply do not care. It’s a treat to spend a little time in one of their enchanting worlds.<br /><br />The secondary character in <i>Ransom</i> were simply amazing. They were as captivating and richly developed as the two main protagonists. I couldn’t seem to get enough of the interactions between Gillian and Brodick’s gruff and intimidating Buchanan soldiers. The scenes between the soldiers and the heroine made for some of the funniest and endearing moments in the story. I also liked Ramsey’s and Bridget’s side story. However, I was a little disappointed with their HEA. It felt abrupt, rushed, and somewhat out of place. They really should have had their own story. It’s sad that didn’t happen for them.<br /> <br />Like most of Julie Garwood’s books, the ending was a bit over the top and eye roll worthy. But hey, that’s signature Julie Garwood and I wouldn’t have it any other way! <br /><br /><i>Ransom</i> is one of the better Julie Garwood books I’ve read. It’s longer than most of her books, with over 500 pages, but it’s full of wonderfully developed characters, action, suspense, humor, and “gasp,” a little angst. <br /><br />I fully enjoyed reading this book and would say it’s a definite keeper. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2676820773649953252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_36569728" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36569728" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36569728?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Scottish highland historical romance lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2015-dangerous-hero-challenge">2015-dangerous-hero-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=own-audiobook">own-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-or-autobuy-author">favorite-or-autobuy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2015-cover-to-cover-challenge">2015-cover-to-cover-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=scottish">scottish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=aar-top-100-romance">aar-top-100-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=kindle-book">kindle-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36569728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16726165586808721923">Another book I thought I had read. Boy was I glad that I didn't. Read this for the Julie Garwood group read, and it was delightful. Julie Garwood books are definitely comfort reads. She understands why we read romance, and one of the reasons is we want heroines who we can root for, that we fall in love with just as much as the heroes. Her heroines have this tangible sweetness that makes me want to hug them, root for them, and to fight with and for them. Gillian is no different. My heart hurt for</span>
  <span id="freeText16726165586808721923" style="display:none">Another book I thought I had read. Boy was I glad that I didn't. Read this for the Julie Garwood group read, and it was delightful. Julie Garwood books are definitely comfort reads. She understands why we read romance, and one of the reasons is we want heroines who we can root for, that we fall in love with just as much as the heroes. Her heroines have this tangible sweetness that makes me want to hug them, root for them, and to fight with and for them. Gillian is no different. My heart hurt for her losses and I cheered her for her indefatigable will. To be honest, I did think she was a slightly too good for Brodick, although I did like him. Maybe that's a good thing, because the common dilemma for a romance fan is to like the hero more.<br /><br />I have read the other two Highland Laird books and loved them. I don't know how this fell through the cracks! But it was perfect timing, because you need a pick-me-up sometimes when you've been reading for so long, and some of it's assigned reading. I am a die-hard romance lover, and while I enjoy other genres, I always come back to romance because it has the tried and true things that satisfy me as a reader. In this case, it's the great heroine and the story that completely immerses me and takes me away from my world--back to medieval Scotland. The romance is great, but there's so much more in addition to offer in this book.<br /><br />One of the things that spoke to me strongly was the theme of family and loyalty. Gillian has lost more of her family, but she cleaves to that which is left. She lived with the hope of being reunited with her sister. Her uncle who raised her after the betrayal and death of her father has her unswerving loyalty. She faces great danger to keep him safe from her so-called guardian Baron Alford, who is essentially the Son of Satan. That doesn't mean she won't spare the time to protect a young Scottish boy who was kidnapped by Baron Alford's forces, even at the risk of her own life. She does it for because it's right, even if it's a great cost to her. Fortunately, her good deed leads her right where she needs to be, and into the sights and arms of Brodick, Laird of the Buchanans.<br /><br />Brodick doesn't know what hits him (not unusual for a Garwood heroine). Before he knows it, he can't live without Gillian, even though he knows from the beginning that she's bound to return to England. He fights his love for her because he believes love makes him weak. Although he hypocritically demands Gillian's love as his due. Brodick takes her into his clan literally, and gives Gillian the family she's missing.<br /><br />Brodick was a pretty good hero. Not good enough for Gillian, but I liked him. I didn't like that he tended to usurp Gillian's self-will, both because he believes he knows better, and also for her protection. He knew that she needed a protector, but the lie he told was a costly one, nearly losing the love of his life in the process. <br /><br />This book has almost two romances for the price of one. The second romance between Ramsey and Brigid was fun, and it develops more slowly than the one between Gillian and Brodick. Most of the characteristic humor is evident in their interactions, since Gillian's situation is so serious, it doesn't leave as much time for humor.<br /><br />Not only was the romance good, but it had genuine suspense. Gillian is in some very dangerous situations, and she makes it through between a combination of divine providence, will power, and intelligence. She hasn't had an easy life, but it's made her into the wonderful heroine she is. One who can't help but acquire the loyalty of those around her.<br /><br />I was more than satisfied with this book. It took me a while to read, but that's sort of my life now. But every time I picked it up, I was deeply involved and enthralled. This was a long book, but when it ended, I wished for more. I did feel disappointment with the resolution of Gillian's search for her sister, but that's real life. And at least she found a new sister in Brigid. I can't help but give it five stars under those circumstances. Even with my increasingly stingy ratings, I can't argue myself down from there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16726165586808721923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671003364" href="/book/show/1023589.Ransom">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tammy / Readers who like epic-like medieval romances</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/939365-eastofoz?shelf=highlander">highlander</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/939365-eastofoz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16386992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2336504169826726967">Excellent! A+! A suberb medieval epic!!! The book is one huge mother of a read but you barely feel it as the pages go whipping on by. <br/><br/>You get two top notch alphas Highlanders: Ramsey and Brodick both lairds of their clan. They get what they want when they want except maybe the women they really love so they have to resort to trickery --especially Brodick-- to seal the deal with their lady loves. The word play in one marriage scene is so well-done that the reader feels like the heroine and doesn'</span>
  <span id="freeText2336504169826726967" style="display:none">Excellent! A+! A suberb medieval epic!!! The book is one huge mother of a read but you barely feel it as the pages go whipping on by. <br /><br />You get two top notch alphas Highlanders: Ramsey and Brodick both lairds of their clan. They get what they want when they want except maybe the women they really love so they have to resort to trickery --especially Brodick-- to seal the deal with their lady loves. The word play in one marriage scene is so well-done that the reader feels like the heroine and doesn't know which end is up or what just happened! Garwood has an amazing talent to write such a long book and never once do you feel bored or get that "read that" before feeling. <br /><br />There's a great group of villains and some outright hilarious scenes. These men are all alpha but in different ways. Ramsey is polite and diplomatic (but don't get him mad) Brodick is frank and forthright and doesn't care who he offends. Do not even think of crossing them when their heroines are in danger. When you think of "alpha hero" these guys certainly come come to mind! <br /><br />Lots of action, great steam, fantastic characters, well-paced ---a true historical romance in every sense!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2336504169826726967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1581300246" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer11451547183591894983">Was this 5 star literature? No, but it sure is 5 star enjoyable. It's campy at times and I doubt the historical accuracy <i>"and you know what?"</i> I didn't care. I was so happy to get Brodick's story and Gillian was lovable despite being so perfect. I won't say much about this as it's been reviewed a zillion times. It's pure fantasy, but it kept me absorbed and put a smile on my face.<br/><br/>Susan Duerden was a fabulous narrator, as usual. </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1581300246">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_537427644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537427644" />
    <a title="Lover of Romance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance"><img alt="Lover of Romance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458253423p2/3709091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537427644?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lover of Romance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lover of Romance" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance">Lover of Romance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=favorites-shelf">favorites-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=top-favorites">top-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=scottish-highlands">scottish-highlands</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537427644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6648193747537931900">Summary <br/>Gillian was just a child when her home was attacked, and her sister disappeared, and her father murdered in front of her, and the Baron Alfred took over and sent her away to her uncle up to northern England. Now its been ten years and she has been called back to the Baron, who wants to know the location of a box that belonged to King John, and thinks that the family still has possession over it. When she plans a escape with a child, Alec, who falls down a gorge, and she rescues him, they</span>
  <span id="freeText6648193747537931900" style="display:none">Summary <br />Gillian was just a child when her home was attacked, and her sister disappeared, and her father murdered in front of her, and the Baron Alfred took over and sent her away to her uncle up to northern England. Now its been ten years and she has been called back to the Baron, who wants to know the location of a box that belonged to King John, and thinks that the family still has possession over it. When she plans a escape with a child, Alec, who falls down a gorge, and she rescues him, they are caught by Baron’s men, and in order to protect the boy, Gillian is severely beaten. And they escape knowing if she doesn’t find the box or her sister the Baron will kill her uncle, a man that is her only family, and was like her own father and raised her, and she will do anything to save him. Gillian and Alec make their way to Scotland, to Brodick Buchanan, who is Alec’s protector and close friend to Alec’s father. Gillian and Brodick are drawn together by circumstances, and even though her life is in England, and she must return there, her heart belongs to a fierce Scot who would protect her at all costs…but will it be enough?<br /><br />The Hero <br />Brodick Buchanan is now laird over th Buchanan’s who are known as heathens among the Scots. Brodick, once wanted a English lass, but when he and his friend Ramsey when to England in search of some sweet passionate lasses, they found none that they liked and were both used. Ever since he made a promise to himself that he would never marry a English lass only a Scottish lass. But when he hears of a woman claiming to be his bride, he is intrigued, and finds himself drawn to Gillian, who is so different from any other woman he has ever known. Brodick is a hoot for a hero….he is one of the most fiercest Scots, and always wearing a scowl, most women fear him, but not Gillian. His character is quite amusing, because he is used to issuing commands and having them obeyed and no protests allowed, I loved his stubbornness, strength, and ways he manages Gillan.<br /><br />The Heroine <br />Gillian has only known pain and grief, she loved her family, but when she witnesses her father being killed right in front of her, her life changed. Gillian as a child, was quiet and kept to herself, and had nightmares. As a woman, she has grown into herself, and is self assured and confident. She stands up to the Baron, and doesn’t let him weaken her resolve. She is protective of those innocent and those she loves most. She is patient with Alec (who is a child with endless questions and she never loses her temper…so bravo) She stands her own ground again Brodick, and isn’t afraid to disobey or disregard his rules he sets down. She is determined to save her uncle, no matter the risk to herself.<br /><br />Plot and Story Line <br />For quite some time I have been wanted to re read Julie Garwood’s historical romances. Now of all the authors that write historical romance, Julie Garwood is at the top. Its been years, so I decided to download the audio version, and the narration was amazing and did the accent quite wonderfully. (And as a side note its on sale at Audible for $3.49–which is quite a bargain so I recommend heading over there while the price is so low.) Ransom is the second book in series, and I recommend if you haven’t read this series yet, you might want to read Secret first since it’s a bit connected to Ransom. The story begins with some background information on our heroine, we see her as a child and a bit traumatized as well from what she witnesses. My heart just went out to her, but then we skip ahead and see her as a woman, and her character was so endearing. She is one of those heroines that accepts what has been dealt to her, but she also stands on her own and fights for what is right. Then we get an added element of a side character, Alec. And for those who have read Secret Alec is Ian and Judith’s son. And what a precocious child he is, and one of my favorite side characters I have ever read. I love the way that Gillian is with him, protects him and even though her uncle is at risk, will return him home as her first priority. And there were so many moments in this story that were charming. What I loved most about this story was the development of characters and seeing the various changes unravel in the plot that keeps the reader engaged. We also have a side love story of Ramsey and Bridgid…and oh Bridgid…just loved her. What I loved most about her character, is that she will only marry one man…the man she loves, but he has to stop “being stupid” before she will even agree. I love her bluntness and how true to herself she is, and holds nothing back. She is brave and bold and I admired that quite a bit and she brought a bit of fresh air to the story. This just might be one of my favorite books from this author, I am sure I read it ages ago when I first started reading romance, but I just don’t remember this one, but now I have decided it’s definitely going to be considered a re listen to. I would recommend it to anyone that loves a tender and fierce love story. A must read for any romance lover–HIGHEST PRIORITY!!!<br /><br />The Cover <br />Now there are two covers for this book, the paper version and the audio version. I like both, but I like the audio version a bit more, since it connects with the setting of the story a bit more.<br /><br />Overall View <br />Ransom is a treasure of charming characters, thrilling plot, quick-witted humor, a tale of love and brings a spicy fresh quality to it, a engrossing read that will have you stunned from beginning to end!! A RICH AND A TRUE DELIGHT!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6648193747537931900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_617514346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/617514346" />
    <a title="Lisa Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay"><img alt="Lisa Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534570690p2/2459470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/617514346?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Kay" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay">Lisa Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781469261270" href="/book/show/15949916-ransom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=well-narrated">well-narrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=re-read-via-audio">re-read-via-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=series-h">series-h</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=m-audible-dot-com">m-audible-dot-com</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-j">authors-j</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=challenge-nbrc-tower">challenge-nbrc-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=amazing-secondary-characters">amazing-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=2013-rlftci-group-challenge">2013-rlftci-group-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer617514346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16844255483743426012"><i>Castle on the cliffs of Scotland</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791922i/556606.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>★★★★★ (This is a review of the audiobook.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3132865.Susan_Duerden' title='Susan Duerden' rel='nofollow noopener'>Susan Duerden</a> has quickly become one of my favorite narrators. In <i>Ransom</i>, one of my favorite Garwood books, she manages to elevate it even more! Awe-mazing. <br/><br/>I’ve read <i>Ransom</i> several times, but it was fun to hear it read to me. Ms. Duerden does a wonderful job on the Scottish accents and inflecting just the right tone for the characters and the situation. I don’t know how she got some of the deep voices for the men. Her pa</span>
  <span id="freeText16844255483743426012" style="display:none"><i>Castle on the cliffs of Scotland</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791922i/556606.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>★★★★★ (This is a review of the audiobook.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3132865.Susan_Duerden" title="Susan Duerden" rel="nofollow noopener">Susan Duerden</a> has quickly become one of my favorite narrators. In <i>Ransom</i>, one of my favorite Garwood books, she manages to elevate it even more! Awe-mazing. <br><br>I’ve read <i>Ransom</i> several times, but it was fun to hear it read to me. Ms. Duerden does a wonderful job on the Scottish accents and inflecting just the right tone for the characters and the situation. I don’t know how she got some of the deep voices for the men. Her pacing and voice level are consistent. It was a real joy to listen to this on audiobook. I’m so glad I didn’t resist getting this newly released version, as I know I’ll listen to it again and again.<br><br>What can I say about a classic Garwood Highland Medieval and – at 546 pages, or 16 hours on audio – a “chunkster” to boot? I feel like I’m repeating myself about Ms. Garwood; but, while there were a few LOL moments, what I really found was that I was <b>smiling</b> throughout this book. I like smiling while I listen to a story; it gives me a warm feeling; makes me want to hunker down under my covers and stay there, indulging in a bit of escapism to Garwood’s Medieval Scotland. This writer can get away with a subtle brand of humor that others cannot. The prologue in this one is excellent, and instantly transported me there. Even in the urgency and danger of the situation JG still managed to capture the character and innocence of a young Gillian and make me… well, smile. ☺<br><br>Here we get two love stories in one, which some people don’t like, but I found one complimented the other and made the developing friendship between the two women, Gillian and Bridgid, a more realistic relationship. It gave them something to talk about. (Not that there wasn’t enough action, intrigue, and betrayal going on in the story.) This was true for the corresponding relationship between the two long-time comrades and heroes, Brodick and Ramsey. They all got to know each other on a different level, and it is easy for me to see the four of them remaining friends for life.<br><br>That said, I felt the resolution of secondary love story was a bit too quick; greedy romance reader that I am, I would have liked a smidgen more. Maybe a wedding? One not on horseback? LOL!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61115974" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61115974?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Kay" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay">Lisa Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=genre-romance-historical">genre-romance-historical</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61115974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14483885485743590993">★★★★½ I read this, the second in the <i>Highlands’ Lairds</i> series, years ago and thought I’d give it another go to see if it still held up. (It does!) There was also going to be a “buddy read” – something I find hard to resist, since I love a good discussion about a great book.<br/><br/><i>My image of green eyed, brown-haired Gillian.<br/>Picture by artist, <b>Cris Ortega</b>.</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379784006i/452607._SX540_.png' width='210' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Thank you, <b>Pamela(AllHoney)</b>, one of my “buddy read” group, for introducing me to this talented artist.<br/><br/>What can I say about a classic Garwood Highland </span>
  <span id="freeText14483885485743590993" style="display:none">★★★★½ I read this, the second in the <i>Highlands’ Lairds</i> series, years ago and thought I’d give it another go to see if it still held up. (It does!) There was also going to be a “buddy read” – something I find hard to resist, since I love a good discussion about a great book.<br><br><i>My image of green eyed, brown-haired Gillian.<br>Picture by artist, <b>Cris Ortega</b>.</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379784006i/452607._SX540_.png" width="210" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you, <b>Pamela(AllHoney)</b>, one of my “buddy read” group, for introducing me to this talented artist.<br><br>What can I say about a classic Garwood Highland Medieval and –at 546 pages – a “chunkster” to boot? I feel like I’m repeating myself about Ms. Garwood; but, while there were a few LOL moments, what I <i>
  <b>really</b>
</i> found was that I was <i>
  <b>smiling</b>
</i> throughout this book. I like smiling while I read; it gives me a warm feeling; makes me want to hunker down under my covers and stay there, indulging in a bit of escapism to Garwood’s Medieval Scotland. This writer can get away with a subtle brand of humor that others cannot. The prologue in this one is excellent, and instantly transported me there. Even in the urgency and danger of the situation JG still managed to capture the character and innocence of a young Gillian and make me… well, smile. ☺<br><br>Here we get two love stories in one, which some people don’t like, but I found one complimented the other and made the developing friendship between the two women, Gillian and Bridgid, a more realistic relationship. It gave them something to talk about. (Not that there wasn’t enough action, intrigue, and betrayal going on in the story.) This was true for the corresponding relationship between the two long-time comrades and heroes, Brodick and Ramsey. They all got to know each other on a different level, and it is easy for me to see the four of them remaining friends for life.<br><br>That said, I felt the resolution of secondary love story was a bit too quick; greedy romance reader that I am, I would have liked a smidgen more. Maybe a wedding?<br><br><i>My image of Bridgid on her wedding day; I guess, Ramsey is the frog, LOL! Picture by artist, <b>Cris Ortega</b>.</i><br><a href="http://s1205.photobucket.com/albums/bb438/LKC55/?action=view&amp;current=Bridgid_on_her_wedding_day311309.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325128i/691000._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And I felt JG missed a golden opportunity with Alec, the child that was kidnapped, when he spit after each utterance of King John’s name. To an appalled Gillian, he explained that Brodick did this too (or cursed); yet, when Brodick does mention King John later – there’s no spitting, cursing or any attempt to refrain from either. Granted, a very small flaw, but I was looking forward to the imagined scene.<br><br>Still, an almost flawless delivery of a sweet and spicy romance. I’ll have to read it again in another couple years to see if it still holds up then.<br><br>Any excuse. **hee hee**<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14483885485743590993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText3287520756940104618" style="display:none">Wow I laughed a lot during this read which balanced out how many times I wanted to throttle Brodick. These brooding men who show their love but won't claim it till the end take my heart on a thrilling ride. I one moment want to cry with the heroine then the next I'm swooning all over again. Gillian was so enjoyable and funny. I liked that she didn't hold her feelings back. These two just worked for me. I really got angry at Brodick so many times but he kept making it right in his neanderthal way. Now Ramsey.. I didn't like much at all. I don't even consider his and Bridgid love story safe or really anything special. She had to watch him whore around for years and the only thing I was glad for was he didn't actually end up sleeping with anyone after meeting her but he wanted to and he would have if she didn't stop it. Idiot. Fool. She deserves better. So glad they didn't have a whole story. He was just disgusting. Good friend.. But bad hero. <br />I really wish I could read about a celibate hero or non "rake" type. <br />Now I'm hooked so I'll be moving into the next read. <br /><br /><br />Safety<br />Brodick and Gillian were totally safe. No ow or om. He's an alpha who takes. Low steam. But really beautiful story.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246436294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14269064548055228349">So I've read another one of Julie Garwood's historical romance books and again I'm both disappointed and satisfied at the same time.<br/> <br/>I don't know why she does this. She starts great, but then she kind of loses her mojo and she rushes things trough, and <i>Ransom</i> is no exception.<br/> <br/>I loved the beginning, I liked how she took time to introduce the heroine, how she talks about her childhood, about the thing that happened when Gillian was 4 years old. I loved how protective Gillian is about the young boy</span>
  <span id="freeText14269064548055228349" style="display:none">So I've read another one of Julie Garwood's historical romance books and again I'm both disappointed and satisfied at the same time.<br> <br>I don't know why she does this. She starts great, but then she kind of loses her mojo and she rushes things trough, and <i>Ransom</i> is no exception.<br> <br>I loved the beginning, I liked how she took time to introduce the heroine, how she talks about her childhood, about the thing that happened when Gillian was 4 years old. I loved how protective Gillian is about the young boy that evil baron kidnapped and how she helped him escape. Her relationship with the boy is adorable and was very well done. To make the long story short, I loved the beginning even thought it took forever for Gillian to actually meet the hero Brodick.<br>When they finally do meet it's lovely, sexy and sweet. Brodick is the typical Garwood alpha male....yum, I love her alpha heroes (especially the Highlanders), he resists and resists and resists, but eventually he realizes that he fell for her from the beginning. Gillian is sweet and naive and innocent, yet so very strong and brave and resourceful. This is what I love about Garwood's books. She writes the best heroines and heroes. Her heroines are headstrong but definitely not bitchy. Usually when I'm looking for a HR to read so many times I stumble upon books where the heroine is often described as fiery and headstrong, but when I actually pick up those books most of the time those heroines seem bitchy and whiny. <br>Garwood's heroes are the best too. The heroes are as alpha as they get, they are sexy and gruff and definitely not very happy about falling in love with the heroines, but when they do fall they fall hard.<br>The chemistry....oh, this woman sure does know how to make the sparks fly. And the marriage ceremonies in Garwood's books are usually very funny and imaginative (remember Judith and Ian's wedding from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret</a> , and Brenna and Connor's wedding from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107778.The_Wedding" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wedding</a> or Madelyne and Duncan's from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107774.Honor_s_Splendour" rel="nofollow noopener">Honor's Splendour</a>?) So of course there's a funny wedding ceremony in <i>Ransome</i> too. Actually it's my favorite of Garwood's wedding ceremonies.<br>Like I said, Garwood sure can write a funny and sexy book, so why, why, why! does she keep switching from <i>show</i> mode to <i>tell</i> mode to <i>show</i> mode to <i>tell</i> mode....and so on. <a href="http://photobucket.com/images/banging%20head%20against%20a%20wall" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364846ra/716630.gif" alt="Small-Stick man banging head against wall Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>At times the <i>show to tell</i> switch is subtle, but it's there.<br>And why does she switch to <i>warp speed</i>? It' like she wants to put all these things in the book but realizes that if she actually took time to properly develop those subplots her books would be at least 200 pages longer. But she doesn't want to exclude those subplots so she crams too many information on one single page that it looks ridiculous. She keeps retelling the story about how Gillian saved the boy, over and over again. We've read the <i>saving the boy</i> part in details at the time she was actually saving the boy, and we read about it again when Brodick finds out about it....but do we need to read it all over again every single time someone new meets Gillian? She's brave and she saved the boy, we know!!!! So move on with it already!!!! <br>And what's with Brigid and Ramsey? Why don't they have their own book? It seems like Garwood was planing to write about them but she decided to cram their story into <i>Ransom</i>, and as a result of that their romance doesn't get the intensity it deserves. Brigid and Ramsey's relationship is a distraction. <br><br>All in all it was a fun book, but it could have been great, and because I love Garwood's heroines and heroes so much it's a <b>3.5</b> stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14269064548055228349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123503712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123503712" />
    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123503712?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671003364" href="/book/show/1023589.Ransom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=historical-romance-prior-to-wwll">historical-romance-prior-to-wwll</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123503712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14390399044384398488">Too annoying to enjoy.<br/><br/>I've read three Julie Garwood novels which were similar: The Secret, Saving Grace and Ransom. All three have an English heroine going to Scotland and falling in love with a Scottish laird. All three women were too saccharine for me. They bring some changes and knowledge to the Scottish people by telling them not to commit certain crimes, to be polite and to have better manners For example one heroine says never steal horses, just borrow them and return them later. One tells</span>
  <span id="freeText14390399044384398488" style="display:none">Too annoying to enjoy.<br /><br />I've read three Julie Garwood novels which were similar: The Secret, Saving Grace and Ransom. All three have an English heroine going to Scotland and falling in love with a Scottish laird. All three women were too saccharine for me. They bring some changes and knowledge to the Scottish people by telling them not to commit certain crimes, to be polite and to have better manners For example one heroine says never steal horses, just borrow them and return them later. One tells the ruling council to give more rights to women. One says a husband doesn't curse in his wife's presence. In two of the books, the heroines bring improved medical knowledge to the Scots. These were too much of the same story and the heroines were too syrupy sweet for me. The heroes were the same, strong, silent warrior types and excellent leaders. In both The Secret and Ransom, the author creates mystery by not having normal communication between the two main characters. In Ransom I was angry at the author for drawing out confusion and mystery through miscommunication. For example, a priest blesses Gillian and Brodick. She thinks it means they are bethrothed (engaged) but the truth is they were married in a method she didn't understand. Later she tells someone she is bethrothed and a soldier says no she is not. If she had then responded to him by asking what the priest had been doing, he would have said that was a wedding. Instead, she says I don't want to talk anymore and walks away. Her not knowing that she was married lasted through several scenes in the book. There were other situations where Brodick would say half of a thought, not finish it and she would assume something incorrect. Or, she overheard part of a conversation, and then assumed something incorrect. Too much of this was happening for me to enjoy the story.<br /><br />Sexual language: moderate. Number of sex scenes: two. Setting: medieval England and Scotland. Copyright: 1999. Genre: historical romance.<br /><br />For a listing of my reviews of other Julie Garwood books, see my 2 star review of "The Secret" posted on 6/21/08.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14390399044384398488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17434694510069397765"><strong>10th read and I still love it</strong><br/><br/>I have read this so many times over the years and I still love it. It's a comfort read and I really needed something to help me through this quarantine. And there's nothing better than a good book. The story is about a very strong woman who is being held by an evil man. She saves the life of Ian Maitland's son who is five years old. Ian was in the book, The Secret which is another all time favorite. The interaction between the heroine and the little boy is so sweet. </span>
  <span id="freeText17434694510069397765" style="display:none"><strong>10th read and I still love it</strong><br /><br />I have read this so many times over the years and I still love it. It's a comfort read and I really needed something to help me through this quarantine. And there's nothing better than a good book. The story is about a very strong woman who is being held by an evil man. She saves the life of Ian Maitland's son who is five years old. Ian was in the book, The Secret which is another all time favorite. The interaction between the heroine and the little boy is so sweet. I loved that part of the story. And then there is Brodrick and he falls for her almost as soon as he meets her. He was very stubborn but so was she and the book captivated me again. There was a side story about Ramsey and Brigite and their blooming love but it was not as good to me. The ending is very abrupt and I wish there was an epilogue. I hate when I leave Garwoods books. I always want more. They are definitely Happy Ever Afters for sure. And a good friend!</span>

Beautiful beyond belief with zero personality. Not even the Viking-like alpha Scottish lairds could make up for that. And while they were your typical HR fare (hard exteriors with ooey, gooey centers) they failed to illicit any real emotion.   <span id="freeText2823310478872068810" style="display:none">I really wanted to love this book but I thought the two female protagonists were both totally bland nitwits. Beautiful beyond belief with zero personality. Not even the Viking-like alpha Scottish lairds could make up for that. And while they were your typical HR fare (hard exteriors with ooey, gooey centers) they failed to illicit any real emotion. So yes, I read every word of every page but I rolled my eyes a million times (that may be a slight exaggeration) and laughed openly at the inconsistency of the characters. Would I read another in the series? You betcha. Not because the books are great quality reads but because HRs are freaking addicting and I'm a sucker for a happily ever after.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2070192575">
  <td colspan="2">

Not my very-most favorite by Julie Garwood, but entertaining, amusing, and smexy.<br/><br/>Gillian was foolish to put herself in harm's way at the end, and I could not believe that she didn't realize what was happening to her, on the horse (snort).   <span id="freeText8003969248432003305" style="display:none">I have read it several times. Some parts are superb! Not my very-most favorite by Julie Garwood, but entertaining, amusing, and smexy.<br /><br />Gillian was foolish to put herself in harm's way at the end, and I could not believe that she didn't realize what was happening to her, on the horse (snort). Her big sister Christen is a self-centered wimp, huh? <br /><br />Of course, as always with Garwood, the characters are absurdly over-the-top, heroes and villains alike. It reads like a tall tale, a "great big fish" story, exaggerated and totally improbable. <br /><br /> But it feels like Garwood knows this, writing with tongue firmly in cheek, and inviting her readers to wink, blink, and go along for the wild ride, with lots of laughs and smexy fun along the way. <br /><br />Plus, gotta love these hunky Highland warriors. ❤<br /><br /> (But Ramsey should have had his own story!)<br /><br />Ps. This is the sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107770.The_Secret__Highlands__Lairds__1_" title="The Secret (Highlands' Lairds #1) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret</a>, featuring Judith Hampton and Iain Maitland. Fun to see recurring characters, but I felt a little sad, too, for the suffering Judith and Iain endured in this book (Ransom). Still, it's a romance, so all's well in the end.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1046490836" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1258837361943401706">As a child, Gillian saw Baron Alford slaughter her father. Her father's guards try to move Gillian and her sister to safety. Her older sister made it to Scotland, but Gillian wasn't so lucky. Now Baron Alford wants to find the King's treasure and believes Gillian knows where it is located. He blackmails her into traveling to Scotland to find her sister and the treasure. But Gillian has a plan. She quickly gains the help of Scottish Lairds Brodick Buchanan and Ramsey Sinclair. With their help and</span>
  <span id="freeText1258837361943401706" style="display:none">As a child, Gillian saw Baron Alford slaughter her father. Her father's guards try to move Gillian and her sister to safety. Her older sister made it to Scotland, but Gillian wasn't so lucky. Now Baron Alford wants to find the King's treasure and believes Gillian knows where it is located. He blackmails her into traveling to Scotland to find her sister and the treasure. But Gillian has a plan. She quickly gains the help of Scottish Lairds Brodick Buchanan and Ramsey Sinclair. With their help and the help of her newest friend, Brigid Kirkconnell, Gillian will bring her fight right back to England and the doorstep of Baron Alford.<br /><br />This is the second book in the Highland's Lairds series. It was a very amusing story with two romances. I wish we could have had a little more time with Ramsey and Brigid. Gillian is a strong heroine who uses her head. Brodick is a big guy who is always scowling and frightens many of the women in his clan. He doesn't scare Gillian at all. My rating: 5 Stars.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1643605499" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643605499" />
    <a title="Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4391611-guilty-pleasures-book-reviews"><img alt="Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490590272p2/4391611.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1643605499?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews" href="/user/show/4391611-guilty-pleasures-book-reviews">Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781439138830" href="/book/show/8869381-ransom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4391611-guilty-pleasures-book-reviews?shelf=guiltypleasures-leigh">guiltypleasures-leigh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643605499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14367988097374920701">Leigh's review posted at <a href='http://www.guiltypleasuresbookreviews.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews</a><br/><br/>FLASHBACK FRIDAY<br/><br/>This one is a blast from the past for me and always has been a favorite of mine. Back during the period when I only read historical romances (and back when that was all she wrote), Julie Garwood was my go-to author for swoon-worthy, funny stories with extreme alpha-heroes and innocent heroines. Her stories have a sweetness in them that I crave, and which are a far cry from the dark erotica I enjoy now. But they just made me gi</span>
  <span id="freeText14367988097374920701" style="display:none">Leigh's review posted at <a href="http://www.guiltypleasuresbookreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews</a><br /><br />FLASHBACK FRIDAY<br /><br />This one is a blast from the past for me and always has been a favorite of mine. Back during the period when I only read historical romances (and back when that was all she wrote), Julie Garwood was my go-to author for swoon-worthy, funny stories with extreme alpha-heroes and innocent heroines. Her stories have a sweetness in them that I crave, and which are a far cry from the dark erotica I enjoy now. But they just made me giggle and sigh and devour the stories in one sitting.<br /><br />Brodick Buchanan is, without a doubt, my favorite of Julie Garwood’s heroes. He’s alpha and Scottish and huge and just plain yummy. Something about him made me adore him from the moment we met him in The Secret (the predecessor to this book), and I couldn’t wait to hear his story. And it did not disappoint. He’s a brute of a laird who is used to bending men to his will, and he finds his match in Gillian, a girl who refuses to be cowed by him.<br /><br />Gillian is the quintessential heroine of Ms. Garwood. She’s naïve, pure at heart, and frankly, a little bit ditzy. But her innocence makes it impossible to dislike her or lump her in the “too stupid to live” category. It would be like hating a kitten. Gillian is funny and plays the comedic role to Brodick’s stoic straight-man.<br /><br />To top off the love story, and storyline of battling against an evil nobleman intent on claiming Gillian’s family home, we also get a bonus romance of Ramsey Sinclair and Bridgid KirkConnell. My only disappointment in this additional couple is that I would have preferred to see them have a book of their own, rather than getting squished in what I perceived to be someone else’s story.<br /><br />For as much as I love this book, readers need to be warned: Ransom needs to be taken with a grain of salt. While in parts it is serious and in parts romantic, it is also downright campy at times. But for years it has always been the re-read that has made me laugh, made me sigh and made me fall in love with Julie Garwood and this particular Scotsman all over again.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14367988097374920701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
